Jamison Brereton

38 (229)
Savitar
Gr╠еtsamada
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn is typically, and in our view rightly, identified as an evening hymn, in which Savitar quiets the world for the night. The hymn is closely analyzed by Falk (1988), who argues that the occasion of the hymn is the evening of the summer sol stice, which marked the beginning of the rainy season. According to Falk, in the sec ond millennium bce on this night the Milky Way rose from the horizon at dusk. The arc of the Milky Way, he says, was pictured as the outstretched arms of Savitar. Be
that as it may, most of the images in the hymn are applicable to evening in general. The first six verses present a lovely series of images of the quiet and rest that evening brings to the natural and the human worldтАФalmost ironically because the daily round of busy movement ceases at the тАЬimpulsionтАЭ of the тАЬImpellerтАЭ (the literal meaning of Savitar). In the following two verses (7тАУ8), SavitarтАЩs ability to bring each creature to its home place at night is extended: he also has assigned to all categories of creatures their proper position in the natural world. The remainder of the hymn celebrates the power of Savitar even over the gods (vs. 9) and asks for his gifts (10тАУ11). The latter verse makes reference to SavitarтАЩs distribution of beings to their separate realms by asking for gifts from heaven, the waters, and the earth. SavitarтАЩs apportioning of benefits in these last verses return us to the theme of the first verse (1cd), which announced his gifts to gods and to the mortal sacrificer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Savitar The word vrat├б- тАШcommandmentтАЩ is prominent in this hymn (vss. 2, 3, 6, 7, 9).

The point is repeatedly made that all creatures, incl. the gods, follow the vrat├б-s of Savitar. Another persistent verbal theme is the contrast between s├бm and v├н (4a, 4c, 6a), which can be discerned even when only v├н is present (1c, 3a, 5b, 6c, 7b, 8d). The hymn also has a pronounced tendency towards augmented 3rd sg. root aorists (+/- preverb) at the ends of p─Бdas, esp. at the ends of hemistichs: 1b asth─Бt, 3d ─Б╠Бg─Бt, 4d ─Б╠Бg─Бt, 5c ─Б╠Бdh─Бt, 6b abh┼лt, 6c ─Б╠Бg─Бt, 8c (─Б╠БтАж) g─Бt, 8d ─Б╠Бkaс╕е, 11b ─Б╠Бg─Бt (cf. also opt.

avy─Бс╕е 10b).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn truth, the divine Savit─Б, the bearer (of the world), has perpetually been present for the genitive ration (of mankind), for such is his office; verily he grants wealth to the pious (worshippers); may he, therefore, bestow upon the offerer of the oblation (sufficient) for his well-being.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

For such is his office: savit─Б = from root su, to bring forth, prasav─Бya lok─Бn─Бm; for such is his work— tadap─Б, tat prasava karm─Б; to the pious worshippers: devebhyaс╕е, to the gods; here interpreted as, stotrbhyaс╕е, to the praisers

Jamison Brereton

God Savitar has stood up to impel again as alwaysтАФthe draft-horse whose work this isтАФ for now he distributes treasure to the gods, and he has also given a
share in well-being to him whose oblations are worth pursuing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb of c, dh─Б╠Бti with primary ending, can only be a root aorist subjunctive like the other two such forms, though neither Geldner nor Renou so tr. it – nor do I. However, Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬтАж soll er тАж verteilenтАЭ does represent the mood (so also Hettrich, Hyp. 177). I would emend the published translation to тАЬwill distribute тАжтАЭ Unfortunately it does not require trisyllabic scansion, which would have supported the subj. interpr.

The question then arises how to analyze ─Б╠Бbhajat in d. The Pp. takes it as ─Б╠Б abhajat, with unaccented augment. Under this analysis the verb would not be in the domain of the h├н in c; otherwise the augment should be accented and the preverb unaccented and univerbated. The Witzel Got┼Н tr. reflects the Pp. by separating the clauses, but Geldner, Renou, and I (implicitly also Klein DGRV II.74) tr. cd as if they contain conjoined parallel clauses. It would also be possible to analyze ─Б╠Бbhajat as ─Б╠Бbhajat, that is, without augment. An injunctive might fit the syntactic context better, in that it could just continue the modal reading of dh─Б╠Бti (тАЬwill distribute тАж and [will] give a share тАжтАЭ), but paradoxically this would require the two clauses to be more independent because the verb would be unaccented and therefore could not be conjoined to c with accent-inducing h├н. In larger interpretational terms the differences among the several possibilities just outlined are fairly minor – having just given or being about to give actually turn out to be almost identical acts in Rigvedic ritual depiction – but it is worth noting the multiple ambiguities inherent in an innocent looking form. For two parallel clauses containing first a subjunctive and then an augmented indicative, see 3ab below (muc─Бti тАж ├бr─лramat).

Griffith

UPRISEN is Savitar, this God, to quicken, Priest who neglects not this most constant duty.
To the Gods, verily, he gives rich treasure, and blesses him who calls them to the banquet.

Dieser Gott Savitri hat sich zum vielten Male aufgemacht, um die Weisung zu geben, der Wagenfahrer, dessen Werk dies ist, denn jetzt verteilt er den G├╢ttern sein Kleinod, und dem Opfereifrigen gew├дhrte er Anteil am Gl├╝ck.

Grassmann

Gott Savitar erhob zu schneller That sich im Flug, aufs neue nun sein Werk zu treiben; Denn jetzt auch theilt den G├╢ttern er die Sch├дtze und schenket Wohlsein dem, der ihn zum Mahl lud.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe divine, vast-handed (Savit─Б), having risen, stretches forth his arms for the delight of all; the purifying waters (flow) for (the fulfilment of) his rites, and this circumambient air sports (in the firmament).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because the god, erect and with broad hands, extends his arms for all to obey,
even the waters are submissive to his commandment and even this wind here rests in its circling.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax n├нmс╣Ыgra- must clearly be a derivative of n├н тИЪmс╣Ыj, lit. тАШwipe downтАЩ, but generally either тАШclasp to oneselfтАЩ or idiomatically тАШdrag downтАЩ (for the latter see I.140.2, V.52.17). The context here requires something like тАШsubmissiveтАЩ, as all tr.

take it. See comm. ad VII.26.3, which suggests that forceful dragging down implies coercion by the agent and, conversely, submission (voluntary or not) of the object.

Note also that it has an unetymological velar g, presumably extracted from forms where the final palatal j, followed by s-, yields -kс╣г-.

The submission of the waters and, especially, the quieting of the wind probably reflect the natural fact that the wind tends to drop at dusk, and this brings about calming of waves that had been raised by the wind.

Griffith

Having gone up on high, the God broadhanded spreads his arms widely forth that all may mark him.
Even the waters bend them to his service: even this wind rests in the circling region.

Geldner

Denn der Gott mit der breiten Hand streckt aufgerichtet die beiden Arme aus, auf da├Я alles ihm gehorche. Auch die Gew├дsser f├╝gen sich seinem Gebote, selbst der Wind rast in seinem Umlauf.

Grassmann

Der Gott steht aufrecht, streckt empor die Arme, thut auf die Hand, und alles lauscht gehorsam; Die Wasser auch, sie schmiegen seinem Dienst sich, und selbst der Wind ruht aus auf seiner Umfahrt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe moving (Sun) is liberated by his rapid rays; verily he has stopped the traveller from his journey; he restraisn the desire of warriors for combat, for night follows (the cessation of) the function of Savit─Б.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The traveller form his journey: or, literally, the goer, from going

Jamison Brereton

Even the one who drives with swift (horses) will now unhitch. He has brought to rest even the wanderer from his travelling.
He has held in check the greed even of the snake-stickers [?]. Following the commandment of Savitar, тАЬReleaseтАЭ [=Evening] has come.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The poet seems to get a certain pleasure out of using semi-exotic verb forms that masquerade as something else: in p─Бda a y─Б╠Бn, the nom. sg. pres. part. of тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ, not the acc. pl. m. of the rel. prn.; in c rhyming ay─Бm╠Р(тЖР ay─Бn тЖР *ay─Бс╣Гst), 3rd sg. s-aor. to тИЪyam. There is also the abl. inf. ├йtoс╕е in b.

The creatures that the hapax ahy├бrс╣гu- (тАШsnakes-stickersтАЩ, Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н), Falk тАШSchlangenspiesserтАЩ, Renou тАШqui picquent les serpentsтАЩ) refers to cannot be determined for certain. The consensus is that it is some kind of bird of prey; Geldner suggests (n. 3c) the Schlangenadler. Indeed, the short-toed snake eagle (Circaetus gallicus) is widespread in India and feeds mainly on snakes (so Wikipedia). The internet (including You Tube) has some remarkable photos and videos of this bird fighting with, swallowing, and feeding its young with snakes, including cobras. The photos with sizable lengths of snake dribbling out of their mouths and esp. the video of one wolfing down a still wriggling spectacled cobra certainly testify to the greed or avidity of these birds. Whether they stop hunting at evening I have no idea.

Griffith

Though borne by swift steeds he will yet unyoke them: e’en the fleet chariot hath he stayed from going.
He hath checked e’en their haste who glide like serpents. Night closely followed Savitar’s dominion.

Geldner

Auch wer mit schnellen Rossen f├дhrt, soll jetzt ausspannen; auch dem Wanderer gebot er Rast vor seinem Marsche. Auch der Fre├Яgier der Schlangenspie├Яer hat er Einhalt getan: Auf des Savitri Gebot ist die Nacht gekommen.

Grassmann

Mit Hengsten fahrend, l├╢st er nun sie wieder, den Wandrer liess er ruhn von seinem Gange, Des Schlangenst├╢ssers rasche Gier bez├дhmt er, auf Savitar’s Geheiss erschien die Nachtruh.

Elizarenkova

рд╡рдпрдиреНрддреА рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдВрд╡рдпрдиреНрддреАрдирд╛рд░реАрд╡ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдГ рд╡рд┐рддрддрдорд╛рд▓реЛрдХрдВ рдкреБрдирдГрд╕рдорд╡реНрдпрддреН рд╕рдВрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯрдпрддреЗ рдкреБрдирдГрд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпреБрд░ рдкреНрдпреЗрд╡рдордХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реАрджрд┐рддрд┐рджреНрдпреЛрддрдпрддрд┐ рдзреАрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮреЛрдкрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрд▓реЛрдХрдГ рдХрд░реНрддреЛрдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрдЩреНрдХрд░реНрдо рдХрд░реНрддреЛрдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡рд╛рдЗрддрд┐ рддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд╕реБрдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН рд╢рдХреНрдо рдХрд░реНрддреБрдВрд╢рдХреНрдпрдордкрд┐ рдордзреНрдпрд╛ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЙрдкрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдЕрдкрд░рд┐рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдиреНрдпрдзрд╛рддреН рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд░реНрдпреБрдкрд░рддрдЗрддрд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрд▓реЛрдХрдГ рд╕рдВрд╣рд╛рдпрд╢рдпреНрдпрд╛рдВрд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрдЙрджрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдЩреНрдХрд░реНрдордХрд░реНрддреБрдВ рдкреБрди рд░реБрддреНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдЬрд╣рд╛рддрд┐рдГрд╢рдпреНрдпрд╛рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗрд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рддрдерд╛рдЪрд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗтАФрдХрд▓рд┐рдГ рд╢рдпрд╛рдиреЛрднрд╡рддрд┐рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рд╣рд╛рдирд╕реНрддреБрджреНрд░рд╛рдкрд░ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рдЕрд░рдорддрд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреБрдкрд░рддрд┐рдГрджреЗрд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЖрдЧрд╛рддреН рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдЙрджреЗ рддреАрддрд┐рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН рдЛрддреВрдиреН рдХрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪрд╡реНрдпрджрд░реНрджрдГ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShe, (Night), enwraps the extended (world) like (a woman) weaving (a garment); the prudent man lays aside the work he is able (to execute) in the midst (of his labour); but all spring up (from repose) when the divine, unwearied Sun, who has divided the seasons, again appears.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Once again the weaver has wrapped up what was stretched out; in the middle of his work the mindful (worker) has set down his craft.
Having pulled himself together, he [=Savitar] has stood up. He has
always kept the seasons separate. As Proper Thinking, god Savitar
has come.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though S─Бyaс╣Зa., Oldenberg, and Renou identify the weaver as Night, this seems unlikely, if the hymn really depicts the evening. More likely a real human weaver, finishing her daily work.

Note the unetym. phonetic echoes in avyat тАж v├бyant─л.

On the semantic and functional nuance of the intensive adardhar, see Schaeffer (Intens., 140-41). The form should be an impf. (see pres. d├бrdharс╣гi), and Schaeffer notes that an the iterative value generally expressed by intensives is not appropriate to an aorist, despite rather insistent aoristic context here. She suggests that ├бdardhar in contrast to the surrounding verbs тАЬbezieht sich nicht auf die unmittelbar vorangegangene Handlung des Gottes, sondern nennt eine T├дtigkeit, die er von alterns vollbracht hat; die Funktion des Intensivums d├╝rfte eine kontinuative sein: тАШsich aufraffend ist er aufgestanden; (fortw├дhrend) hielt er die Jahreszeiten auseinander; bereiten Sinnes ist der Gott Savitr╠еgekommen.тАЩтАЭ My ‘always’ is an attempt at reconciling this.

P─Бda-initial ar├бmatiс╕е тАШProper ThinkingтАЩ echoes p─Бda-initial ├бr─лramat (3b) (see also ramate 2d), though they are of course etymologically unrelated. I now think a pun is meant here, with ar├бmati- analyzed as a privative a-r├бmati- and I would emend the tr. to тАЬAs Proper Thinking (/unresting) тАжтАЭ

Griffith

What was spread out she weaves afresh, re-weaving: the skilful leaves his labour half-completed.
He hath arisen from rest, and parted seasons: Savitar hath approached, God, holy-minded.

Geldner

Die Webende hat das ausgebreitete Gewebe wieder zugedeckt; mitten in der Arbeit hat der K├╝nstler sein Werk niedergelegt. Er r├╝hrt sich und hat sich erhoben; er hat die Zeiten geschieden. Rasch entschlossen ist Gott Savitri gekommen.

Grassmann

Zusammen rollt die Weberin den Aufzug, der K├╝nstler bei der Arbeit gab sein Werk auf; Sich r├╝stend stand er auf und schied die Zeiten, Gott Savitar erschien der nimmer rastet.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рдзреАрд░реЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпрд╛ рдордзреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рдпрдиреНрддреА рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рд╡рд┐рддрддрдВ рд╕рдорд╡реНрдпрддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддреЛрдГ рд╢рдХреНрдо рдиреНрдпрдзрд╛рддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╢рдВ рд╕рдВрд╣рд╛рдпреЛрддреНрддрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рддреНрдпреБрджрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН рддрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рддрд┐ рдпреЛрд╜рд░рдорддрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡ яДДрддреВрдиреН рд╡реНрдпрджрд░реНрдзрдГ рд╕рдиреНрдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдиреН рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдЧрд╛рддреНрддрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рддрд┐ рд╕ рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓рдЦрдЧреЛрд▓рд╡рд┐рджреНрднрд╡рддрд┐ реерекрее

рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рдГ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рд╢реЛрдХрдГ рддреЗрдЬрдГ рджреБрд░реНрдпрдГрдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрдГ рдЧреГрд╣реЗрднрд╡рдГ рдирд╛рдиреМрдХрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐рдпрдЬрдореНрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреГрдердЧреНрднреВрддрд╛рдиреН рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреЗ рдЕрдзрд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдорд╛рдпреБрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдордиреНрдирдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдзрд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рдЖрдпреБрдГ рд╕реВрдиреГрддреЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрдирдирд╛рдорд╕реБрдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН рдорд╛рддрд╛рдЙрд╖рд╛рдГ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рд┐рддрдореНрдкреНрд░реЗрд╖рд┐рддрдВ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрдХреЗрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдХрдВрдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдардореНрдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдЦреНрдпрдореНрднрд╛рдЧрдВ рд╕реВрди рд╡реЗрдЕрдЧреНрдирдпреЗрдЖрдзрд╛рддреН рдЖрджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ рее рел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe engendered domestic radiance of Agni spreads through various dwellings, and presides over all (sorts of sacrificial) food; the mother, (Dawn), has assigned to her son, (Agni), the best portion (at sacrifices), which is the manifestation of him imparted by Savit─Б.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The agnihotra rite is to be performed at dawn, which may be therefore considered as enjoined or instrumental gated by the rising sun

Jamison Brereton

The domestic blaze of fire is dispersed prominently throughout the houses, one for each, for (each oneтАЩs) whole lifetime.
The mother has set out the best portion for her son, according to his intention, which has been aroused by Savitar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

v├н tiс╣гс╣нhate should be evaluated in conjunction with v├нс╣гс╣нhitaс╕е in 6a and v├н tasthuс╕е in 7b.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take a and b as separate clauses (sim. Falk). My rendering is closer to RenouтАЩs. I think the idea is that Agni/Fire, though in some ways a single entity, is parcelled out into separate domestic fires, one per household, and this holds for a manтАЩs whole lifetime after he has set up his household fire. The coming of night brings the (re-)kindling of these fires and so they come into visual prominence then.

The blazing up of the home fire is accompanied by the evening meal, rather charmingly depicted here: the mother reserving the best of it for her son; the son with his appetite stimulated by the coming of evening.

Griffith

Tlirough various dwellings, through entire existence, spreads, manifest, the household light of Agni.
The Mother gives her Son the goodliest portion, and Savitar hath sped to meet his summons.

Grassmann

In H├дusern rings zu allem, was da lebet, vertheilt sich Hauses Feuer hell ergl├дnzend; Das beste Theil legt vor dem Sohn die Mutter, weil Savitar ihm die Begier erregt hat.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe warrior, eager for victory, who has gone forth (to battle), turns back; (for) home is the desire of moving beiings; abandoning his half-wrought toil, the labourer returns (home) when the function of the divine Savit─Б (is suspended).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Whatever) was dispersed seeking gain has been gathered together. Desire for home has arisen in all who roam.
Each and every one has come, abandoning unfinished work, following the commandment of the divine Savitar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda of this vs. takes up the idiom v├н тИЪsth─Б тАШdisperseтАЩ found in 5b and applies it somewhat differently. Here it refers to all those who were dispersed in various directions pursuing their livelihoods – who all want to come home in the evening. On jig─лс╣г├║- see Narten (Yasna H., 122); as she makes clear, the desid. of тИЪji in both Vedic and Avestan lacks martial or battle context and is simply about gaining food and so on. See also Heenen (Desid. 120-25).

The verb sam─Б╠Бvavarti is taken by K├╝mmel (465-66) as a (pseudo-)passive aor. to тИЪvс╣Ыt, with ref. to Hoffmann (Aufs. II.589-92), a form that is attested also after the RV (see K├╝mmel n. 884). The lexeme s├бm-─Б╠БтИЪvс╣Ыt is used in the causative of DawnтАЩs cows rolling up the darkness (VII.79.2), so here I think the nuance is the gathering or rolling up together of everything that was dispersed during the day, playing on the common opposition between v├н and s├бm that is prominent in this hymn.

Although we might expect v├нkс╣Ыtam to mean тАШbadly/wrongly doneтАЩ, I think the dominant s├бm / v├н play in this hymn trumps that, and if s├бс╣Гskr╠еta- is тАШperfected, brought to completionтАЩ, v├нkrta╠е - can mean тАШincomplete, not doneтАЩ.

Griffith

He comes again, unfolded, fain for conquest: at home was he, the love of all things moving.
Each man hath come leaving his evil doings, after the Godlike Savitar’s commandment.

Geldner

Wer auf Gewinn ausgezogen war, kehrt heim; aller Wanderer Wunsch ging heimw├дrts. Jeder lie├Я die Arbeit halbgetan liegen und ist heimgekehrt nach dem Gebot des g├╢ttlichen Savitri.

Grassmann

Es kehrt zur├╝ck, wer zu erwerben ausging; die Sehnsucht aller Wandrer strebte heimw├дrts; Sein Werk verlassend gehet heim ein jeder, auf das Geheiss des g├╢ttlichen Erregers.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗрд╕рд╡рд┐рддреНрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБрдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдЖрдкрдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрддрд┐рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдирд╛рдорд╕реБрдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН рдЬрд▓рд╛рдзрд╛рд░реЗрд╡рд╛рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐ рддрдВ рдЕрдкреНрдпрдордкрд╛рдВрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдореНрднрд╛рдЧрдиреНрдзрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрдирд┐рд░реНрдЬреНрд▓рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢реЗрд╖реБрдЕрд░рдгреНрдпреЗрд╖реБрдореГрдЧрдпрд╕реЛрдореНрд░реБрдЧрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ рдореГрдЧрд╛рдГ рдЖрд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рд╡рд┐ рд╡рд┐рддрд╕реНрдереБрд░рдзрд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рднреНрдпрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд┐рднреНрдпрдГ рдЖрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкреЗрдгрддреНрд╡рдпрд╛рднрд╛рдЧреЛрджрддреНрддрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╕рд╡рд┐рддреБрдГ рддрд╛рдирд┐рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐рдирдХрд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рдирдиреНрддрд┐ рдХреЗрдкрд┐рдирд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe animals search in dry plural ces for the water element which has been collected in the firmament by you; the woods are assigned (by you) to the birds; no one obstructs these functions of the divine Savit─Б.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The watery (race) has been placed by you among the waters; the wild beasts have been dispersed throughout the wastelands, as their share; the forests are for birds. No one violates these commandments of god Savitar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In my view, this vs. divides the world into habitats for fish (etc.), wild beasts, and birds. Not surprisingly the watery creatures are placed in water (p─Бda a). As head noun with ├бpyam I supply j├бnma from the summary p─Бda of this two-vs. sequence, 8d.

The problem in 7a is bh─Бg├бm: it is tempting to tr. тАЬthe watery (race) has been placed by you among the waters as their share,тАЭ but bh─Бg├бm belongs to a masc. stem and must be acc., which does not accord with the nominal clause in which it would purportedly be found. I therefore construe this last word of p─Бda a with b, as an appositive to acc. pl. dh├бnva тАШwastelandsтАЩ. Although I would prefer to avoid such enjambment, I see no better choice, and note that a new clause also begins in the middle of p─Бda c (with n├бkiс╕е) and continues to the end of d. Sim. also 9c. GeldnerтАЩs interpr., which keeps bh─Бg├бm within its p─Бda by making the whole p─Бda acc., seems to me to come at too high a cost: he must supply a set of fishermen and a verb тАШseekтАЩ to govern the acc. (тАЬ[Fisherman seek] their watery share ..тАЭ); these imaginary fishermen are parallel to the тАЬhuntersтАЭ that he takes mс╣Ыgay├бsaс╕е to be, dispersed across the dry land (and presumably hunting wild beasts). I see several conceptual problems with this interpr. For one thing this makes the first two p─Бdas non-parallel with c, for there are no bird-catchers there (Vedic Papagenos?), whereas in my interpr. the three p─Бdas describe the habitats of three types of creatures. Moreover, the hunting has no obvious connection with Savitar, whereas by my interpr. the distribution of habitats is his doing - and is summed up by 8d тАЬSavitar has distributed the races according to their stations.тАЭ Nor is the hunting likely to be an activity of night, the other thematic connection it might have to the rest of the hymn: everyone else has gone home, but hunters are out on the plains trying to shoot deer in the dark? For penetrating arguments against the Geldner interpr. see OldenbergтАЩs n. 3 ad loc. P─Бda b has its own problem, the anomalous form mс╣Ыgay├бsaс╕е. Geldner (n. 7ab) declares that mс╣Ыgay├бs- can only mean тАШhunterтАЩ, but gives no evidence for his certainty. OldenbergтАЩs disc. is more to the point (and rather tart about the тАШhunterтАЩ interpr.), though his morphological analysis of it as an -as-derivative of the denom. mс╣Ыgayseems a little shaky (likewise his alternative explan. as a cmpd. of loc. mс╣Ыg├й + тИЪas тАШshootтАЩ, like hс╣Ыtsv-├бs- [see Scarlatta 41], with older sandhi and a meaning тАШauf das Wild schiessendтАЩ, which unfortunately smuggles in GeldnerтАЩs hunters in another guise). On the other hand, I donтАЩt have anything better to offer. It reminds us of a suffix-accented masc. deriv. like rakс╣г├бs- тАШdemonтАЩ next to neut. r├бkс╣гas- тАШdemonic forceтАЩ, which itself gets personified. But the assumed base *mс╣Ы╠Бgayas- (or *mс╣Ыg├бyas-) тАШwild-beast-inessтАЩ doesnтАЩt exist and itтАЩs hard to see to what it would be generated. AiG II.2.223 dismisses the word with a ? and a ref. to OldenbergтАЩs disc. In any case, OldenbergтАЩs structural arguments that it must refer to the beasts, not the hunters are sound. A third occurrence of v├н тИЪsth─Б is found in this p─Бda.

The asya in p─Бda c anticipates dev├бsya savit├║с╕е in d - perhaps better to tr. as Geldner does: тАЬтАж diese seine Gebote, des Gottes Savitar.тАЭ This doubling may have arisen because the clause begins in the middle of a p─Бda and continues over the p─Бda break.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. have been variously interpr. My interpr. is most influenced by Oldenberg (whose views also seems to have been adopted by Witzel Got┼Н). As noted in the published

introduction, the vss. enumerates the separate spheres assigned to the various categories of creatures by Savitar, as an extension of his ability to bring every creature to its proper resting place at night.

Griffith

The wild beasts spread through desert places seeking their watery share which thou hast set in waters.
The woods are given to the birds. These statutes of the God Savitar none disobeyeth.

Ihren von dir bestimmten, im Wasser liegenden Anteil suchen die Fischer im Wasser; die Wildj├дger zerstreuten sich ├╝ber das trockene Land. Die B├дume sind f├╝r die V├╢gel: Nicht verfehlen sie diese seine Gebote, des Gottes Savitri.

Ins Wasser setztest du des Wassers Erbtheil, und auf dem Festland rings vertheilt das Wild sich; Den V├╢geln gabst den Wald du, nie verletzen sie dieses Gottes Savitar Gebote.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ever-going Varuс╣Зa grants a cool, accessible and agreeable plural ce (of rest), to all moving (creatures) on the closing of the eyes (of Savit─Б), and every bird and every beast repairs to its lair when Savit─Б has dispersed (all) beings in various directions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

On the closing of the eyes of Savit─Б: Varuс╣Зa especially presiding over the night

Jamison Brereton

As far as (SavitarтАЩs) benefit extends, Varuс╣Зa (has come) to his watery womb, restlessly darting about at (every) blink (of the eye).
Every mortal creature, (every) domestic beast has come to its pen.
Savitar has distributed the races according to their stations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The general purport of this vs. is clear: it both summarizes SavitarтАЩs distribution of the creatures (esp. in p─Бda d) and hints (esp. in p─Бda c) at their return to their own special places at night. But the first half-verse is quite challenging and my interp. is not fully worked out.

On y─Бdr─Бdhy├аm see OldenbergтАЩs disc. My published translation тАЬAs far as (SavitarтАЩs) benefit extendsтАЭ is, IтАЩm afraid, opaque. What it means to convey is that Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs presence in his watery womb is at the favor of Savitar, whose distribution of the creatures in their proper places extends even to the gods, or at least one of them. A modern equivalent might be the phrase тАЬto serve at the pleasure of (e.g.) the president.тАЭ The dependence of Varuс╣Зa (and other gods) on SavitarтАЩs orders and ordering is stated plainly in the next vs., 9ab. It is esp. striking that Varuс╣Зa follows SavitarтАЩs vrat├б-, since the vrat├б- is primarily Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs domain. That Varuс╣Зa is the only god named here is probably meant to emphasize what might almost be seen as SavitarтАЩs usurpation of the power and role of Varuс╣Зa. SavitarтАЩs r─Б╠Бdhas- recurs in 11b.

This passage shows one of the early examples of what becomes Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs principal association, that with water. Again, it may be that Savitar is deliberately relegating him to this restricted role. Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs hypervigilance, familiar from other, more standard treatments of Varuс╣Зa in the RV, is undeterred by his watery environment, as p─Бda b indicates.

Note the phonological play in ├бniс╣гitaс╣Г nim├нс╣гi.

The sense of nim├нс╣гi is unclear. My tr. тАЬat (every) blink of the eyeтАЭ takes it as an implicit ─Бmreс╕Нita with the frequenative j├бrbhur─Бс╣Зaс╕е; it could also be an indication of the great speed of Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs movements, like English тАЬin the blink of an eye.тАЭ However it shouldnтАЩt be forgotten that the idiom n├н тИЪmiс╣г is associated with the gods and esp. the ─АdityaтАФgenerally in its negation: the gods (or their spies) тАЬnever blinkтАЭ (cf., e.g., IX.73.4, X.10.8, 63.4). For Mitra and Varuс╣Зa or the ─Аdityas see VII.60.7, 61.3, VII.25.9, and esp. nearby II.27.8 asvapnajo animi ╠Б с╣г─Б╠Б├бdabdh─Бс╕е тАЬunsleeping, unblinking, undeceivableтАЭ (of the ─Аdityas). Is the blinking here (as opposed to the usual non-blinking) another of SavitarтАЩs subtle put-downs of Varuс╣Зa, implying that he does blink after all? In c m─Бrt─Бс╣Зс╕Н├б- is taken by the standard tr. (also L├╝ders, Varuс╣Зa I.50) as тАШbirdтАЩ, and this could work well, corresponding to 7c, where the birds are assigned to the forests. However, note that in vs. 7 the other member of the trio of creatures, besides the watery, is the wild beast (7b), whereas here instead of a wild beast we have precisely a domesticated one, the pa┼Ы├║-. Its formulaic partner is m─Бrt─Бс╣Зс╕Н├б-, lit.

тАШstemming from a dead eggтАЩ, found otherwise in the RV in the creation hymn X.72.8-9 in the myth of Aditi and the birth of her sons. The last son born (or rather the egg miscarried), m─Бrt─Бс╣Зс╕Н├б-, is the ancestor of mortals; for disc. of the word and the myth see Hoffmann 1976 (=1992: 723). That half of this vs. is devoted to Varuс╣Зa and the next vs. has the great trio of AditiтАЩs sons, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and Aryaman, provides further evidence that the M─Бrt─Бс╣Зс╕Нa of the Aditi birth story is meant. Under this interpr., the domestic herd animal (pa┼Ы├║-) is paired with the likewise domesticated human, each in its own pen.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. have been variously interpr. My interpr. is most influenced by Oldenberg (whose views also seems to have been adopted by Witzel Got┼Н). As noted in the published

introduction, the vss. enumerates the separate spheres assigned to the various categories of creatures by Savitar, as an extension of his ability to bring every creature to its proper resting place at night.

Griffith

With utmost speed, in restless haste at sunset Varuna seeks his watery habitation.
Then seeks each bird his nest, each beast his lodging. In due place Savitar hath set each creature.

Geldner

Varuna geht, sobald es m├╢glich ist, in seine Wasserheimat, der rastlos im Augenzwinkern hin und her zuckt. Jeder Vogel ging in sein Nest, das Vieh in den Pferch. Je nach ihrem Standort hat Savitri die Arten gesondert.

Grassmann

So gut er kann, sucht auf den Schooss der Wasser der Fisch am Abend, er, der rastlos zappelt, Des Eies Sohn das Nest, den Stall die Heerde; nach ihrem Sitz schied Savitar die Thierwelt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invite to this plural ce, with reverential salutations, for my good, that divine Savit─Б, whose functions neither Indra, nor Varuс╣Зa, nor Mitra nor Aryaman nor Rudra nor the enemies (of the gods), impede.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whose commandment neither Indra nor Varuс╣Зa, neither Mitra nor Aryaman, nor Rudra violates,
nor do hostile powersтАФfor well-being I call him here with homage: god Savitar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich restates 7cd in almost the same words, but instead of the indefinite n├бkiс╕е тАШno oneтАЩ specified as the non-violator of SavitarтАЩs vrat├б-, a selection of the greatest gods serve as subject.

Griffith

Him whose high law not Varuna nor Indra, not Mitra, Aryaman, nor Rudra breaketh,
Nor evil-hearted fiends, here for my welfare him I invoke, God Savitar, with worship.

Geldner

Des Gebote weder Indra, noch Varuna, Mitra, Aryaman, noch Rudra verfehlen, noch die Unholde, diesen Gott Savitri rufe ich jetzt unter Verbeugungen zum Heil.

Grassmann

Ihn, dessen Satzung Indra nicht, noch Rudra, Varuna, Mitra, Arjaman verletzen, Noch b├╢se Geister, ruf ich her zum Heile, Gott Savitar mit demuthsvollem Herzen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay he, who is adored by men, the protector of the wives (of the gods), preserve us; when worshipping his, who is auspicious, the object of meditation, and the all wise; may we be the beloved of the divine Savit─Б, that we may (thence be successful) in the accusative ulation of wealth and the acquisition of cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The protector of the wives of the gods: gn─Бspati, devatn─лn─Бm pat─лn; or, gnaс╕е = the metres of the Vedas (RV. 5.46.8)

Jamison Brereton

As (we) arouse Fortune, Insight, and PlenitudeтАФPraise of Men, the husband of the Wives, should help usтАФ
might we be dear to god Savitar at the approach of a desirable thing and at the gathering of riches.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner points out (n. 10a), the three divinized principles in p─Бda aтАФGood Fortune, Insight, and PlenitudeтАФare what the poet needs for success.

As the layout of the published translation shows, I take p─Бda b as a parenthetical insertion in the sentence that includes a, cd. It would be possible to take v─Бj├бyantaс╕е as a predicated pres. part. and a separate cl., though this seems less likely to me.

Although gn─Б╠Бsp├бti- presumably contains the old gen. sg. of gn─Б╠Б- (e.g., AiG III.119, 129), I tr. it as a pl., since we usually hear of тАЬwives (of the gods)тАЭ - though, since I donтАЩt exactly know what Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa (=Agni?) is doing here, perhaps thereтАЩs only one wife. It is also not clear if there are two figures here or if gn─Б╠Бsp├бtiс╕е characterizes Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa as I have taken it (so also Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н). Renou does so in tr., but suggests in his n. that it might identify a separate individual, perhaps Tvaс╣гс╣нar, whose association with divine females is well established. I now am inclined in that direction and would provide an alternate tr. тАЬNar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa (and) the Husband of the (divine) Wives should help us.тАЭ That the verb is singular is not an impediment, since a series of sg. subjects can take a sg. verb.

This verb, avy─Бс╕е, is a bit of a problem. It is isolated in the averbo of the root тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ, which is seс╣н and has a well-attested iс╣г-aor. (on which see Narten 86-89) beside the even better attested them. pres. Although Narten (86) identifies our avy─Б╠Бс╕е (also X.139.5) as belonging to an old root aor. (with maintenance of the full grade despite despite being opt.), there are no other unambig. root aor. forms attested (though forms like ─Б╠Бv─лt could of course belong to a seс╣н root aor. paradigm and have given rise to the iс╣г-aor.). I think itтАЩs more likely an artificial form, makeshift replacement for the non-existent iс╣г-aor. opt. (see my 2009 тАЬWhere Are All the Optatives?тАЭ pp. 31-32 on the absence of act. sigmatic optatives, flg. Narten), as well as the relative dearth even of 3rd sg. thematic optatives to present stems (like ├бvati), on which see the same art., pp. 32-34.

As for the point of the p─Бda: it is possible that the arousing of the three principles in p─Бda a reminds the poet that he needs the help of the ritual fire (if Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa is identified with Agni here). Perhaps gn─Б╠Бsp├бtiс╕е is invoked because two of the three principles are female. But this seems like groping in the dark.

Griffith

May they who strengthen bliss, and thought and wisdom, and the Dames’ Lord and Narasamsa aid us.
That good may come to us and wealth be gathered, may we be Savitar the God’s beloved.

Indem wir Bhaga, die Dhi, die Purandhi aneifern - Narasamsa, der Herr der G├╢tterfrauen, m├╢ge uns dabei helfen - m├╢chten wir die Lieblinge des Gottes Savitri sein, wann Gut einkommt und Reicht├╝mer sich ansammeln.

Gl├╝ck, Andacht, Reichthum m├╢gen wir beeilen, der Herr der Frauen Nar─Б├зana helf’ uns; wo Gut sich zeigt, und wo sich Reichthum anh├дuft, da sein in Savitars, des Gottes, Huld wir.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗрд╕рд╡рд┐рддрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдиреНрддреНрд╡рдпрд╛рджрддреНрддрдиреНрддрддреНрдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдЩреНрдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдВ рдХрдордиреАрдпрдВрд░рд╛рдзреЛрдзрдирдиреНрджрд┐рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рддреН рдЕрджреНрднреНрдпреЛрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рддреН рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рднреВрдореЗрд╢реНрдЪрдЖрдЧрд╛рджрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рд╕реНрддреЛрд╕реНрддреГрднреНрдпрдГрд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдорд╛рдкрдпреЗрдмрдиреНрдзрд╡реЗ рддрджреНрд╡рдВрд╢рдЬрд╛рдп рдпрджреНрдзрдирдВ рд╢рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░рдореНрднрд╡рд╛рддрд┐рднрд╡реЗрддреН рдЙрд░реБрд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рдпрдмрд╣реБрд╕реНрддреБрддрдпреЗрдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗрд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗрдорд╣реНрдпрдВ рдЬрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдХрд╛рд░реБрд░рд┐рддрд┐рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрдирд╛рдорд╕реБрдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН рд╣реЗрд╕рд╡рд┐рддрдГ рддрддреНрдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫ рее резрез реердЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгреЗрд╡реЗрддреНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрд░реНрдЪрдВрд╕рдкреНрддрдордВрд╕реВрдХреНрддрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рд░реНрддреНрд╕рдорджрдиреНрддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдорд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рдгреЗрд╡рд╛рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирдорд┐рддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрдЧреНрдпреЗ рднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реЗрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдкрдЯрд▓реЗрд╕реНрдпрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдЮреНрдЪтАФрдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгреЗрд╡реЗрд│реЗрджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд░ рдкреАрджрдВрд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдЮреНрдЪтАФрдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгреЗрд╡рдирд╛рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐рддреНрд░реАрдгреАрддрд┐ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that desirable wealth which is granted to us, Savit─Б, by you, proceed from the sky, from the waters from the earth; and may the happiness (which belongs) to the race of those who eulogise you, devolve upon me, repeating diligently your praises.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

That desirable benefit given by you has come to us from heaven, from the waters, from earth,
(a benefit) that will become weal for your praisers and your friend, the singer whose recitations extend widely, o Savitar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb ─Б╠Бg─Бt is interpr. by the Pp as injunc g─Бt and so treated in most editions and tr., but it could just as well be augmented ag─Бt, a typical aorist in a summary vs. [II.39 JPB]

Griffith

So come to us our hearts’ desire, the bounty bestowed by thee, from heaven and earth and waters,
That it be well with friends and those who praise thee, and, Savitar, with the loud-lauding singer.

Geldner

Uns soll vom Himmel, vom Wasser, von der Erde als dein Geschenk diese erw├╝nschte Ehrengabe zukommen, die den S├дngern Gl├╝ck bringen soll und deinem Freunde, dem Lobredner, dessen Worte weithin dringen, o Savitri.

Grassmann

Uns fliesse zu von Himmel, Erd’ und Wassern begehrenswerthes Gut, von dir geschenktes, was Segen bring’ den S├дngern und dem Freunde, o Savitar, und dem, der laut dich preiset.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрдГ) рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдорд╣рддреНрддрддреНрддреНрд╡, рдорд╣рддреНрддрддреНрддреНрд╡ рд╕реЗ рдЕрд╣рдВрдХрд╛рд░, рдЕрд╣рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрддрдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛, рдкрдЮреНрдЪрддрдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдУрдВ рд╕реЗ рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдБ рдФрд░ рд╕реНрдереВрд▓ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрднреВрдд рдФрд░ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рдпрд╛рдБ рдмрдирд╛рдИрдВ, рдЬрд┐рдирд╕реЗ рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░, рд╕реВрд░реНрдп, рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЕреЬрддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рддреАрд╕рд░рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рджрддреНрддрдВ рджрд┐рд╡реЛрд╜рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдпрддреН рдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдВ рд░рд╛рдзреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдорд╛ рдЧрд╛рддреН рддрджреБрд░реБрд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рдп рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдЖрдкрдпреЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╢рдВ рднрд╡рд╛рддрд┐ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН) (рддрддреН) рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдВ рдЬрд▓рдореН (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╛рддреН (рдЕрджреНрднреНрдпрдГ) рдЬрд▓реЗрднреНрдпрдГ (рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рднреВрдореЗрдГ (рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛) (рджрддреНрддрдореН) (рдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдореН) рдХрдордиреАрдпрдореН (рд░рд╛рдзрдГ) рдзрдирдореН (рдЖ) (рдЧрд╛рддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рд╢рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рдпрддреН) (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ (рдЖрдкрдпреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдп (рднрд╡рд╛рддрд┐) рднрд╡реЗрддреН (рдЙрд░реБрд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рдп) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдп (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрдГ) (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рдЕрд░реНрдЪрд┐рддрд╛рдп реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЗрдг рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╛ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рдорд╣рддреЛрд╜рд╣рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реЛрд╜рд╣рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН рдкрдЮреНрдЪрддрдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛рднреНрдп рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕реНрдереВрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪреМрд╖рдзрдпреЛ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рддрд╛рдГред рдпреИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд╛рдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ реерезрез рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
